field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson is meant to help students distinguish between the proper roles of science and theology in a Catholic worldview. Students will understand that science and theology complement one another in comprehending the universe and humanity’s purpose within it.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Understand that science is a systematic and logical approach to discovering how things in the material universe work.  (https://www.livescience.com/20896-science-scientific-method.html)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Understand that theology is a systematic and logical study of the nature of God and religious belief.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Understand the respective roles of science and theology in the Catholic worldview.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Students will be able to explain to one another why there should not be conflict between theology and science.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Students will be able to describe an example of religious error or superstition and/or scientific idolatry or false absolutes and discuss how the example represents an overreach of its own discipline.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Students will be able to apply this idea to something they have heard or experienced in their own lives.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span>Hook (10 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>A student (selected ahead of time) presents a popular song to the class.  </span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>Follow-up discussion: (Have students discuss the first set of questions for two minutes in small groups, then share out with the class.  Then show the second set of questions and allow for small group discussion and share out time.  It is possible that most students won’t know the answers to the questions in the second set.)</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>Why</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> do you like the song?  How do you feel when you listen to it?  What about the song makes you like it (or not like it)?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>How</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> is music made?  How do you hear it?  What are sound waves?  Why are some notes a different pitch than other notes?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Big Idea: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Science and theology, when properly applied, are not in conflict because they answer different questions.  </span></em><span>For example, s</span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>cience can describe how an instrument plays, how we hear it, and even why some combinations of notes sound good together and not others, but it can not discuss the aesthetics of the music, the feelings it evokes, or the composer who wrote it (because the composer is not him/herself within the piece of music).  In a similar way, science can describe structures and processes in the material universe, but can not tell you anything</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>about why the universe exists, can not quantify its beauty, and can not prove or disprove a Creator who exists outside of the material realm.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> Wrap-up quote: p</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>. 7 of </span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>Creation: A Catholic’s Guide to God and the Universe</span></span></span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span> </span></em></span></span></span></span></span>  <span><span><span><span><span><em><span>​​​​​</span></em><span>“Science takes things apart to tell us how they work; religion brings things together to show us what they mean.”  But St. John Paul II said it first; in his words, “ the theological teaching of the Bible, like the doctrine of the Church… does not seek so much to teach us the </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><strong><span>how</span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> of things, as rather the </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><strong><span>why</span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> of things.”</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Goal Statement:  Today we are going to investigate the proper roles of science and theology and look at examples of common mistakes when either one oversteps its bounds.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><strong>Main lesson (30-35 min)</strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><em><span> In his letter to the Director of the Vatican Observatory, St. John Paul II asserted that, “Science can purify religion from error and superstition; religion can purify science from idolatry and false absolutes. Each can draw the other into a wider world, a world in which both can flourish.”</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p>What are some examples of errors or superstitions within religion that science can help purify?  What does idolatry and false absolutes look like in science?</p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>I Do:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Religious Error: Flat earth (Isaiah 40:22,</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> He sits enthroned above the circle of the earth, and its people are like grasshoppers. He stretches out the heavens like a canopy, and spreads them out like a tent to live in.</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>)  </span></span></span></span></span></span><em><span><span><span><span><span><span>How do we know that the author is not attempting to convince the reader that the Earth is flat? What is the author’s point in this passage?</span></span></span></span></span></span></em><span><span><span><span><span><span><em> </em> (Maybe discuss poetic language vs. historical narrative in the Bible.)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Religious Superstition: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> A superstition that still has traction in modern culture is astrology.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><em><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Can science help debunk astrology?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></em><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Video:  Why astrology isn’t real science.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VZ2eMUmumw0"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VZ2eMUmumw0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Scientific idolatry and false absolutes:  Carl Sagan said, “I am a collection of water, calcium, and organic molecules called Carl Sagan.”  </span></span></span></span></span></span><em><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is missing in Dr. Sagan’s description of himself?  What is he inferring about the universe (and God)?</span></span></span></span></span></span></em></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>We Do:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Religious Error: the sun revolves around the earth (Joshua 10:12-14 At that time Joshua spoke to the Lord in the day when the Lord gave the Amorites over to the sons of Israel, and he said in the sight of Israel, “Sun, stand still at Gibeon, and moon, in the Valley of Aijalon.” And the sun stood still, and the moon stopped, until the nation took vengeance on their enemies. Is this not written in the Book of Jashar? The sun stopped in the midst of heaven and did not hurry to set for about a whole day. There has been no day like it before or since, when the Lord heeded the voice of a man, for the Lord fought for Israel.)  </span></span></span></span></span></span><em><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is the author trying to convey in this passage that the Sun revolves around the Earth?  If not, what is the author’s point in these verses?</span></span></span></span></span></span></em><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Scientific idolatry:  Richard Dawkins said, "Religions do make claims about the universe -- the same kind of claims that scientists make, except they're usually false."   </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><em><span><span><span><span><span><span>Does religion and science attempt to answer the same questions?  What is Mr. Dawkins’s apparent position concerning religion in general?  Is his stance scientific or philosophical?</span></span></span></span></span></span></em></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Positive examples of when faith and science are properly applied:  </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://watch.formed.org/the-search-1/season:1/videos/thesearch-ep3"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://watch.formed.org/the-search-1/season:1/videos/thesearch-ep3</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> - (11:10-15:10)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>George LeMaitre - Father of the Big Bang Theory</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Roger Bacon - Grandfather of the scientific method</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Nicolas Copernicus - Pioneered Heliocentrism</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Jean-Baptiste Lamark - Prefigured evolution with theory of Lamarckism</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Friar Gregor Mendel - Pioneer of Genetics</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Father Angelo Secchi - Father of Stellar Spectroscopy</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>All of these scientists were Catholic priests and religious who studied science to find out how the world works and devoted their lives to God who is the reason why they had life. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Karin Ingegerd Öberg is a </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Swedish astrochemist and</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Professor of Astronomy at Harvard University.  She leads the Öberg Astrochemistry Group at the Harvard-Smithsonian Center for Astrophysics. She is also an adult Catholic convert. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Karin studies how our solar system was formed, how the earth became inhabitable,  how other planets form and the likelihood of finding other living planets.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Quote from Karin from the video “I find modern cosmology is probably telling us something about the personality of the Creator.  It seems we have a God who wants the universe to participate in creating. Often unexpected structures appear but still in accordance with the laws of nature. I think that the world exists at all points to the fact that there is a Creator who created the world.  I think the beauty of the cosmos points toward the Creator that is beautiful and values that beauty.  The intelligibility of the world points to an intelligent creator.”</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p>Revisit the big idea from the "Hook" portion of the lesson:</p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science tells us how the universe was made &amp; faith tells us why the universe was made.  Seeing these truths together gives us a fuller understanding of the universe than either of the truths could show separately. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Other ways to apply - Faith tells us that God gave us a body as a gift and we should take care of this gift.  Science can tell us how to take care of the body by telling us what foods are healthy and what helps the body to be well. Seeing these two truths together gives us a greater understanding of the gift of the body. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Summary quote:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Joseph Ratzinger, Homilies 1-4, pp. 1-78, </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>In the Beginning: </span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>A Catholic Understanding of the Story of Creation and the Fall</span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>p. 18 “ The reasonableness of the universe provides us with access to God’s Reason and the Bible is and continues to be the true enlightenment … because it opened reason to God’s truth and love.”</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Summary assessment at end of class (or as homework):</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>1)  Based on the above examples of a scenario of the proper role of science and theology, with your groups, brainstorm a real world example from your lives of ways to apply the proper role of science and theology.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>2)  Individually write a paragraph telling the proper role of science and theology and an example of how they can work together.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>3)   Write one question you still have about the harmony of faith and science.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><br /> <span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>Answer key for in-class questions:</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>From the “Hook” section:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>How</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> is music made?  How do you hear it?  What are sound waves?  Why are some notes a different pitch than other notes? </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Music (and all noise) results from the vibration of an object such as vocal cords or instrument strings.  The vibrations push air particles back and forth, creating air pressure differences called compressions and rarefactions that get propagated through air.  When those compressions and rarefactions strike one’s eardrum, they get magnified by the bones of the middle ear and transcribed into nerve signals that the brain detects as sound.  Higher pitches are produced when an object vibrates faster and lower pitches come from slower vibrations, so high-pitch instruments tend to be smaller and lighter whereas low-pitch instruments are larger and heavier.</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>From the “I Do” section:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Religious Error: Flat earth (Isaiah 40:22,</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> He sits enthroned above the circle of the earth, and its people are like grasshoppers. He stretches out the heavens like a canopy, and spreads them out like a tent to live in.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>)  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>How do we know that the author is not attempting to convince the reader that the Earth is flat? </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>The author is obviously using poetic language.  He does not literally view the sky as something flexible like a tent or people as grasshoppers.  The language is poetic, not literal.</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is the author’s point in this passage? </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>The overall message of Isaiah 40 is one of comfort and hope for God’s people.  The frailty of mankind is contrasted with the greatness of God.  The author was just highlighting the transcendence of God using poetic language.</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Scientific idolatry and false absolutes:  Carl Sagan said, “I am a collection of water, calcium, and organic molecules called Carl Sagan.”  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is missing in Dr. Sagan’s description of himself?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Sagan makes no mention of consciousness or soul.</span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is he inferring about the universe (and God)?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Sagan is inferring that the material universe is all that exists.  There is no soul and no God. </span></em></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>From the “We Do” section:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Religious Error: the sun revolves around the earth (Joshua 10:12-14 At that time Joshua spoke to the Lord in the day when the Lord gave the Amorites over to the sons of Israel, and he said in the sight of Israel, “Sun, stand still at Gibeon, and moon, in the Valley of Aijalon.” And the sun stood still, and the moon stopped, until the nation took vengeance on their enemies. Is this not written in the Book of Jashar? The sun stopped in the midst of heaven and did not hurry to set for about a whole day. There has been no day like it before or since, when the Lord heeded the voice of a man, for the Lord fought for Israel.)  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is the author trying to convey in this passage that the Sun revolves around the Earth?  If not, what is the author’s point in these verses? </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>The point of this passage is best summarized in the last 5 words: “the Lord fought for Israel”.  This was written as an example of a supernatural miracle showing God’s protection and provision for the Israelites.  No attempt is made by the author to explain how this might have happened and he was in no way trying to make a scientific statement about which celestial bodies revolve around which others. </span></em></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Scientific Idolatry:  “Religions do make claims about the universe – the same kinds of claims that scientists make, except they’re usually false.”</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Does</span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> religion and science attempt to answer the same questions?  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>No.  As you have hopefully been learning in this lesson, theology and science are two different ways of investigating reality.  Science investigates the material world, theology the spiritual.  This is a fundamental flaw in Mr. Dawkins’s objections to religion.</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is Mr. Dawkins’s apparent position concerning religion in general?  </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Richard Dawkins is an atheist… and very outspoken about spreading his atheism to the world.</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is his stance scientific or philosophical?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>This quote is an example of scientific idolatry because it is attempting to use science as a substitute for religion when, in fact, they investigate two different aspects of our existence.</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder callback="flag.link_builder:build" arguments="0=node&amp;1=293&amp;2=favorite_lessons" field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">The properties of water show the splendor of the Creator. How are the unique properties of water that allow for life signs of a thinking/knowing/logical Creator? Using St. Thomas Aquinas’ 5 Intellectual Proofs for the existence of God, specifically #5 “Grand Designer” students will examine how water behaves the way it does because of the biological/chemical processes necessary for life to function. Students will further understand the role of water in sacred scripture and tradition.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong>1. </strong>Further describe how God is the “grand designer” through order and lawfulness.</p> <p><strong>2. </strong>Students are able to articulate that water is extraordinary</p> <p><strong>3. </strong>Recognize the role of water in Sacred Scripture and Tradition</p> <p><strong>4.</strong> Identify properties of water</p> <p><strong>5.</strong> Recognize that the fields of science and religion compliment to show the majesty and order of the universe. (and <strong>are not</strong> in conflict)</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Evaluate, analyze &amp; synthesize evidence of God as the Grand Designer by applying concrete evidence.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate proper lab procedure</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Understand (and possibly analyze depending on depth of student responses) properties of water</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Analyze a concept through a science and faith lens (cross-curricular)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Understand that water is important in sacred scripture and Catholic tradition</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Evaluating Information through research</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>NOTE: the students should have read St. Thomas Aquinas' 5 Proof's of God's Existence prior to completing this lesson.</p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Starter</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>On the board the teacher will have the following written: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>Water: Ordinary or Extraordinary?</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span> </span></em></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> TSW complete a 5 minute quick write on the topic. No discussion but the class will circle around to it at the end. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teacher: Reviews St. Thomas Acquinas’ Proofs, focusing on #5: God as Grand Designer (Order and Lawfulness of Universe) See ppt resource if necessary. Teacher states: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span>Water is one example of the manifestation of order and lawfulness, which points to the existence of an all-wise God.</span></em></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Hand out Anticipation Guide (Resource) and have students complete </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Before Column </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>to assess prior knowledge on water in Sacred Scripture and water’s scientific properties</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>.</span></em></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Body </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="4"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>TEACHER LEAD IN: “</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span>God reveals his existence to us through the created order that science studies.  Through God’s activity as the “Grand Designer”, we can see beauty, symmetry, and power in our world that leads us to see a manifestation of law and order.  One excellent example is the unique properties and characteristics of water.”</span></em></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The teacher will present the PPT: </span></span></span></span></span></span><strong><span><span><span><span><em><span>What is the Role of Water in Sacred Scripture &amp; Tradition</span></em></span></span></span></span></strong><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>.</strong> (See resource)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>(Teacher Asks Students)</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span> “So now, what are the order and properties of water that convey the splendor of God’s creation?”</span></em></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> The teacher will show a short video (created by science teacher; see resources) to show the several qualities of water that show order, beauty, majesty. </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>(Examples: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>reactant in photosynthesis, product of respiration and combustion, capillary action in xylem, cell physiology, dissolved oxygen for sea life respiration, freezing of water allowing sea life to survive, heat of fusion and vaporization, etc.)</span></em></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>TEACHER REITERATES:  If water did not have these properties, life as we know it would not be able to exist.  Water expands when it freezes which allows ice to float on liquid water unique to this molecule.  This allows for sea life and allows large bodies of water to be on earth.  Water has a very large specific heat and heat of vaporization.  If these values were smaller, earth’s temperatures would not be as stable and there would be too much water vapor leading to cloud cover and rough meteorological conditions. From a theological viewpoint, this uniqueness is evidence of how a molecule is so perfect for the sustaining of life with all of its unique properties, that it </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>is a very strong</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> evidence of an all-wise Creator. Furthermore, the pattern/properties of water demonstrate St. Thomas Aquinas’ 5th proof: God as the “grand designer” – order, beauty, majesty.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Physical demonstrations: To show visually what the video describes; the teacher will complete two physical demonstrations [labs] with students.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teachers can use the hotplate to demonstrate that water has a high specific heat.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The teacher will fill a large metal bowl with room temperature water. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>A PASCO thermometer will be placed in the bowl of water.  Students will be able to see the temperature of the water on the projector screen.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The thermometer will now be placed on the outside of the bowl, so that students can see the temperature of the bowl is the same as the water in the bowl.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The hotplate will now be turned on.  After 1 minute the temperature will be taken in the bowl of water, and then again in the bowl of water.  Students will now be able to see that the bowl of water has not heated up as quickly as the outside of the bowl. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The teacher will then ask the students which properties of water have just been shown. (Answer:  Specific Heat, heat of vaporization)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teacher can use xylem demonstration with a capillary tube</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The teacher will give each group of two students a watch glass.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will add 4 drops of water to the  watch glass, and then 1 drop of food coloring.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will touch the small puddle of water with the end of the capillary tube.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will observe the liquid rise in the capillary tube.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The teacher will then ask the students which properties of water have just been shown. (Answer: cohesion, adhesion)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Assessment/ Extension</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="9"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>TSW return to their Anticipation Guide (from starter) and answer the same statements on water in the “after column” and turn in as a formative assessment. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li>If there is time or teacher would like additional assessment; have students return to their Quick Write on Water being Ordinary vs. Extraordinary and complete another 5 minute write.</li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>EXTENSION: TSW research other examples of God as the “grand designer” (order and lawfulness of the universe) as shown by something in the natural world or scientific study. [Teacher note: Such as an element (like water),a process (gravity), a specific scientific study (astronomy), etc.] (see resource)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Closing:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>To conclude the lesson the class will pray.   </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(Holy Water would be bonus but is not required)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Church teaches about the sacredness of life and the dignity of the human person. Water is essential to life, but almost 1 billion people don’t have access to clean water. God of Creation, On the third day you caused water to fall from the heavens. And it was good. Ever since, water has been essential to our life, to our health and to our very existence. Our rivers and streams teem with life. Our forests, and farms and meadows, are rich in vegetation because of the rain you send down and the springs that you raise up. We are grateful and humbled by it. And sometimes we are fearful of it. We acknowledge water’s strength, its ability to flood, to devastate, to drown, even as we praise you for water’s gift of life, and sustenance and growth. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Help us to be worthy stewards of this great gift, to make sure that none go thirsty. Help us to safeguard its purity, accessibility and beauty. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>We pray that each time we wash our hands, pour water in a glass or water the lawn, we will say a prayer of gratitude for clean water and be reminded to act and pray on behalf of those who live without it. We pray that each time we bless ourselves with holy water or see the baptismal font, we will be inspired to live out our baptismal call to follow Jesus’ example and uphold the dignity of others, especially those who live without clean water. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>We pray all this (signal everyone to dip their fingers in the holy water and make the sign of the cross together) in the name of the Father, and of the Son and of the Holy Spirit.  Amen</span></span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Quick Write on Water: Ordinary or Extraordinary (pre-assessment) -- If revisit at end of lesson can also be used as formative assessment.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Anticipation guide that includes pre-lesson responses and post-lesson responses (formative assessment)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Extension: Research on other examples of God as the “Grand Designer” in the natural and scientific world. (summative assessment)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder callback="flag.link_builder:build" arguments="0=node&amp;1=285&amp;2=favorite_lessons" token="toeIuC0Mw1AI1g-s9TzNt7mBF827HFdsXe558dQAlJE"></drupal-render-placeholder> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-resources--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-resources.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-resources.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-resources field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Lesson Resources</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Copies for students: Anticipation Guide</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Copies for students: Extended Research Assignment w/ Rubric</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>PPT: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>What is the Role of Water in Sacred Scripture &amp; field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Essential Questions</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Since the existence of God is revealed by the orderliness and majesty of the universe, how do the properties of water convey the splendor of God’s creation?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What are the characteristics of water that give it its extraordinary properties?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is the essential role of water for sustaining life on Earth?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is the role of water in Sacred Scripture and Tradition? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson’s focus is to introduce students to different types of knowledge that can be gained through the study of science and that of Christian theology. Through this guided lesson, students will be able to describe that science can answer the “how” questions while Christian theology can answer the “why” questions. Students should also recognize that both types of knowledge are necessary for a complete understanding of our world. <br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1. Recognize the type of questions that can be answered by science and theology.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>2. Describe what it means for science to be looking ‘at’ a problem to gain knowledge as described in “Meditations in a Toolshed”</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>3. Demonstrate an awareness of the limitations of science.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>4. Describe what it means for science to be looking ‘along’ a problem to gain knowledge as described in “Meditations in a Toolshed”</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>5. Demonstrate an awareness of the limitations of theology.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>6. Articulate the Catholic understanding of the Bible.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Differentiate between scientific and theological knowledge in a source.  </span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Describe the purpose of the scientific method in gaining knowledge of the natural world</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Compare and contrast the purpose of knowledge gained through theology versus science.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Read and interpret Genesis 1:1-13 in the Christian Tradition. </span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Draw connections between truth revealed through science and truth revealed through Theology</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Lesson Timing:  1- 55 minute class in the freshman/sophomore science class/ 1- 55 minute class with discussions/activities for the freshman/sophomore religion class portion</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 1: Science Class  (55 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Do Now: Google Form</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What types of questions do you want science class to answer this year? What do you recall of the scientific method? (5 mins)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Scientific Method refresher (5 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read "Meditation in the Toolshed" Excerpts and "Meditation" blog summary (10 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> Discussion to distinguish between “looking at” and “looking along” (5 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Make a TikTok video (choice of 3) and then watch the video. Making TikTok = looking along, watching TikTok = looking at (8 min–5 to do activity)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Flat Earth TikTok (Trust your Eyes) viewing (1 min) and analysis Tennis ball meme. When we mistake looking ‘along’ for looking ‘at,’ we fail to properly do science.  (3 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>How </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>do we know that the earth is round? Video and reading (8 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>"Meditation" Review  (3 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Exit ticket on Google form – (8 min) </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Based on what we have talked about with looking 'at' something through science, which of the following questions can science answer? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>In your own words and complete sentences, tell me what it means for science to look at the light, like in the "Meditation" passages?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 2: Religion Class (55 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Do Now: Google Form</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is your personal perspective on the Bible? What kinds of questions would you look to religion to answer? (5 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>TikTok and Meditation in the Toolshed recap (5 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reading of Genesis 1:1-13 </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Drawing of the world based on Gen. 1 (10 min) </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ancient Worldview (firmament) picture and connection with observation, How vs. Why of a text (5 min) </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read Pope Benedict Excerpts (pages 4-5) (12 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discussion on the purpose of the creation accounts vs scientific accounts (coriolis effect, degrees…) (10 min). </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Exit Ticket </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What knowledge do you hope to gain from a Religious book like the Bible? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How can scientific understanding enhance this theological knowledge? (8 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 1: Science </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pre Assessment: Do now of Scientific Method: </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://forms.gle/i1hTkVdnBAQjN1J3A"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://forms.gle/i1hTkVdnBAQjN1J3A</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Formative assessment During: Class discussion of Scientific Method, Class discussion of “Meditation in the Toolshed,” Class discussion of TikTok dance and Flat Earth.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Formative Post-assessment: </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://forms.gle/KnuGbK4Dhg2m9ew79"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://forms.gle/KnuGbK4Dhg2m9ew79</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This is a lesson that will provide students with an overview of how genetics and chromosomes function. It will encompass genetic information, DNA, codes for the formation of proteins, the process of mitosis, chromosomes, and potential abnormalities. Students will consider the connection with the science of God’s intentions and human dignity and whether or not we should interfere with genetics.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>All cells contain genetic information in the form of DNA molecules. Genes are regions in the DNA that contain the instructions that code for the formation of proteins.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>In multicellular organisms individual cells grow and then divide via a process called mitosis, thereby  allowing the organism to grow. The organism begins as a single cell (fertilized egg) that divides successively to produce many cells, with each parent cell passing identical genetic material (two variants of each chromosome pair) to both daughter cells. Cellular division and differentiation produce and maintain a complex organism, composed of systems of tissues and organs that work together to meet the needs of  the whole organism.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="3"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Each chromosome consists of a single very long DNA molecule, and each gene on the chromosome is a  particular segment of that DNA. The instructions for forming species’ characteristics are carried in DNA. All  cells in an organism have the same genetic content, but the genes used (expressed) by the cell may be  regulated in different ways. Not all DNA codes for a protein; some segments of DNA are involved in  regulatory or structural functions, and some have no as-yet known function.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="4"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>In sexual reproduction, chromosomes can sometimes swap sections during the process of meiosis (cell  division), thereby creating new genetic combinations and thus more genetic variation. Although DNA replication is tightly regulated and remarkably accurate, errors do occur and result in mutations, which are also a source of genetic variation. Environmental factors can also cause mutations in genes, and viable mutations  are inherited. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="5"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Environmental factors also affect expression of traits, and hence affect the probability of occurrences of traits  in a population. Thus the variation and distribution of traits observed depends on both genetic and environmental factors.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be able to:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Use a model to illustrate the role of cellular division (mitosis) and differentiation in producing and maintaining </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>complex organisms.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask questions to clarify relationships about the role of DNA and chromosomes in coding the instructions for </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>characteristic traits passed from parents to offspring.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Make and defend a claim based on evidence that inheritable genetic variations may result from: (1) new genetic </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>combinations through meiosis, (2) viable errors occurring during replication, and/or (3) mutations caused by </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>environmental factors.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Apply concepts of statistics and probability to explain the variation and distribution of expressed traits in a </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>population</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>This lesson is one lesson broken into two days (80 minutes per class, total 160 minutes).</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span> </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teacher will use instruction, stopping frequently to check for understanding with the students.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will listen and engage in dialogue with the teacher. When the lesson is finished, the students will copy down the notes from the board.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Making use of the different modules in this unit.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Show video on Creation as an anticipatory set: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pH53AHPXVPU"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pH53AHPXVPU</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1.1 </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Meet:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Biology Teacher and Faith Teacher/or single teacher Introduction.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1.2 </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Growth &amp; Compassion:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Guide students to reflect on events beyond their control. They will be guided to reflect on “compassion” towards those who are different from them.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1.3 </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Our human diversity (the experience): </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students intentionally look at each other’s eye and observe the diversity and the beauty of the human eye; color, shape.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1.4 </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Experience:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Students are guided to build a model of an eye and the teacher teaches them the complex genetics behind the color of the human eye, to understand the possible variations that can exist.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Materials Needed per Student or Pair: </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Foam ball, foam square, foam sheet, stick, </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>google eye or draw it, toilet paper roll, paint glue.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1.5 </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Engage:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Race, Genetics, and Ancestry. Students brainstorm and explore the relationship between genetics, race, and ancestry. They will be guided to understand how appreciating these differences will help to uphold human dignity and rise above prejudices.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1.6 </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Assignment:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Students will be asked if they think there could be consequences for chromosomes being irregular? Those that do will form one group (Pro) and those that do not will (Con) form another group. Students will be given time to do research to defend their position in class and should do any additional preparation needed as homework. Students will debate the two sides Pro/Con in the next class session.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from questions that arise from examining models or a theory to clarify relationships.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Use a model based on evidence to illustrate the relationships  between systems or between components of a system.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Make text-formatted field field--name-comment-body field--type-text-long field--label-hidden field__item"><p>This is a lesson that will provide students with an overview of how genetics and chromosomes function. It will encompass genetic information, DNA, codes for the formation of proteins, the process of mitosis, chromosomes, and potential abnormalities. Students will consider the connection with the science of God’s intentions and human dignity and whether or not we should interfere with genetics.</p> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Students will know</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>There can be no conflict between religious truth and scientific and historical truth (CCC, no. 159)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>the purpose of scientific study</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>the purpose of theological study</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The difference between the Catholic understanding of Scripture and that of those who interpret the Bible in an overly literalistic, fundamentalist way or with an approach limited to a symbolic understanding  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>that Genesis 1–11 conveys religious truth rather than science (CCC, nos. 283-289)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Students will be able to:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Construct explanations (NGSS Science Practice)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Engage in argument from evidence (NGSS Science Practice)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Obtain, evaluate, and communicate information (NGSS Science Practice)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>(with the Church)  relate truths of faith to science</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p> </p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson timing</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Time: Five 80 minute class lessons.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson plan structure</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 1:  </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Learning target: Students will provide understanding of how the natural sciences enrich our understanding of God and his creation, and how theology can enrich our understanding of the natural sciences.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Opening discussion:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask students to write down their own answers to the following: How do people today believe faith and science relate to each other? What are the pros and cons of these various perspectives. How do Catholics approach this question? (20 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Preparatory reading:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The instructor will guide students through reading the preparatory document and answering the questions on their own sheet of paper. (60 minutes) (End class 1)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 2: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Learning Target: Students will provide a deeper understanding of the process of natural sciences </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Opening discussion/Bell work:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Recap the relationship between theology and science that was covered in the preparatory readings by reviewing answers in a whole class discussion. The teacher will lead this by asking every student to respond at least one time (20 minutes, longer if there is a need to re-teach)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Nature of Science class discussion:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><a href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1_YtxJclzrHMjz384n2tsaQIjuxYrhqkb/view?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Nature of Science Notes</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> (40 minutes). The instructor will guide students through the notes on Nature of science and elaborate/field questions as needed to enhance student understanding. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Closing discussion: </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Individual, pair , share. In light of our readings and class discussions, readdress our initial question: What is a scientific view of the created world? What is a theological view of the created world? What are the pros and cons of these various perspectives? How do Catholics approach this question? (20 minutes). </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will record their individual answers and resulting changes through discussion (paper or digital format) so the instructor can collect and identify any misconceptions or questions before returning for Day 3</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 3:  </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Learning Targets: Students will summarize and apply their knowledge of theological and scientific processes to a topic of their choice. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teacher will address any misconceptions or questions from previous work in the lesson (5 min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introduce podcast integration paper assignment - outlined below</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teacher will walk through instructions with students (15 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will select podcasts. Teacher will check in with each student. (15 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will listen to first podcast and take notes and answer questions (45 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>For homework: complete the first part of podcast paper relating to first podcast.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 4: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Learning Targets: Students will summarize and apply their knowledge of theological and scientific processes to a topic of their choice. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Work day:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Each student will listen to his or her second podcast and take notes (50 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will have the rest of class to work on his or her paper (30 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><br />  </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 5: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Learning Target: Students will teach other members of their group what they claimed in the paper</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teacher will place students in groups of four (5 min) and have them complete a provided document as other students in their group teach them about how their podcast answers the questions in the assignment.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div>
