field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This two-part lesson plan is designed to introduce a Christian morality course. The lessons seek to demonstrate how both Biology and Theology, in their own ways, reveal the fundamental truth that humans are relational beings. Students will then consider how to understand Christian morality, specifically the 10 commandments, as a guide to fruitful relationship with God and others rather than a burdensome list of things humans can and can&#039;t do. </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe the function and importance of the placenta</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Articulate how the placenta and fetomaternal microchimerisms exemplify the relational nature of humans</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate familiarity with the Genesis 2-3 narrative</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Articulate how Genesis 2-3 shape the Christian understanding of the relational nature of humanity and the impact of sin on relationship </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain Christian morality in relational terms</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read and interpret Genesis 2-3 in the Christian Tradition </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Draw connections between truth revealed through science and truth revealed through Theology</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Apply claims about human nature to their own lives</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Timing:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></strong><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>2 classes, each class is 75 minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Structure: </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p>Class 1: Human Relationality in Biology</p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Do Now Prompt</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> (Prompt is posted for students as they enter class. They have 5 minutes to brainstorm their responses.): What are some of the most important relationships in your life right now? Do you think it’s possible to find happiness without meaningful relationships? Explain your answer. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Class share/discussion</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>- Encourage 5-6 students to share their Do Now responses. Wrap up the sharing period by emphasizing that we can see from our own experiences how it’s essential to have meaningful relationships in order to live flourishing human lives. This is because humans are relational beings. We’re not meant to be isolated. Explain that the students will explore how both Biology and Theology show us the truth that we are created for relationships. </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Alternative Option- Rather than transitioning directly from individual student reflection to an entire class discussion, you could follow the think, pair, share format. After students brainstorm their own responses, they can turn to a partner and discuss their initial thoughts with each other. Once they talk one-on-one for several minutes, you can transition to a discussion with the entire class. </span></em></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Relationality from a Biological Perspective</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introduce</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>- Pass out “Student Notes Handout” (included in the lesson Files). Explain that they will spend the class focusing on a Biological example of how humans are relational beings. Make them aware that it will feel like a science class. </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Option- Spend a few minutes introducing Dr. Kristin Collier, the doctor in the videos that they will watch. Point out that she is a highly qualified medical doctor who was not Christian for most of her life. </span></em></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Anatomy of the Placenta Video</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Play the first 4:05 minutes of </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XgnfWSqMEZc"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>this video</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> (the link is also included in the Lesson Resources) for the students. Have the students draw a diagram of the uterus, define each of the terms, and jot down notes on the role of the placenta on their notes handout. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Spend several minutes reviewing the material and making sure the students have all the relevant information</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Play the remainder of the video. Have students draw the cross-section diagram of the placenta on their notes handout. They should color or draw the parts of the placenta that are from the mother in one color and the parts of the placenta that are from the baby in a different color. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Spend several minutes making sure all students understand the material. </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Option- Consider giving the students the link to the video and having them watch it on their own. This will allow them to pause and replay the video whenever they need to record information.</span></em></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Microchimerism Video</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Play the first 5:55 minutes of </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oiqNEmoVnZ4"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>this video</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> (also included in the Lesson Resources) for the students. Have students take notes on the basics of microchimerisms. </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Consider pausing the video shortly after Dr. Collier defines the scientific definition of a microchimerism. Repeat and clarify the definition for the students to make sure that they understand before continuing the video. </span></em></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Spend several minutes reviewing the material with the students. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reflection Questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Give students 10 minutes to answer the reflection questions on their notes handout. The teacher can determine if the questions should be done individually, with a partner, or in small groups. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Invite students to share their responses. Emphasize that we are connected and dependent on each other down to the very cellular level. In order to be most fully ourselves, we depend on others. Thus, we have a mutual responsibility towards each other. (See “Student Notes Handout- Answer Key”, which is included in the lesson Files, for additional key points to emphasize.) </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Class 2: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Human Relationality in the Theology</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Do Now Prompt</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> (Prompt is posted for students as they enter class. They have 5 minutes to brainstorm their responses.): </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>As relational beings, we depend on each other down to the cellular level. We’re created to live in community with others. Think of some of the communities of which you are a part (family, athletic team, club, school, parish, town, etc.) Choose one or two of these communities. What are the blessings AND challenges of living in relationship with others within these communities? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pair/Share Do Now Responses</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>- Have students turn to a partner and discuss their initial thoughts. Then invite students to share their reflections with the entire class. Wrap-up the discussion by emphasizing that community is a source of joy and blessing, but it can also be hard to live in relationship with others because it requires us to be open to others and responsive to their needs. The grace of the Sacraments (especially Reconciliation and the Eucharist) can strengthen us to live as better members of the different communities in our lives. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Relationality From a Theological Perspective</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introduce</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Direct students to pull out their student notes handout from the previous class, as well as a Bible. Remind them that last class they saw how humans are interconnected down to the cellular level. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain that in this class they will examine how the Christian Theological Tradition understands human relationality. However, in the Theological Tradition, humans are not only connected to each other, but to their creator. Our need for connection and community is how we image God, who is a community of persons (Trinity). </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Remind the students that Genesis 2-3 is not meant to be a scientific account of creation. It aims to reveal religious truth regarding who God is, the purpose of creation and what it means to be human. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reading and Guided Questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>- Divide students into small groups. Have each group read Genesis 2-3 together, then discuss and answer the guided questions on the student notes handout. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Review and Discuss</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>- Discuss responses to the guided questions together as a class. See “Student Notes Handout- Answer Key” (included in the lesson files) for key points to emphasize as you review with the class. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Concluding Notes</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>- Use the “Concluding Notes” PowerPoint (included in the lesson files) to summarize some key ideas and introduce students to the idea that Christian morality is ultimately about building and protecting proper relationships with God and others. Use Psalm 119:33-35 (second to last slide on the PowerPoint) help students consider how view the commandments as positive things rather than burdens. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Formative assessment at the end of the first class</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>To gauge student understanding, students will answer the following question, which is included in their student notes handout: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>How do the placenta and fetomaternal microchimerisms challenge the idea that each of us is autonomous from the other people in our lives on a biological level? Do you think this should impact the way we view our relationships with others?  </span></em></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Summative assessment</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The following question can be used on a unit 1 Christian morality test: </span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Draw from Biology, Theology, or your own experience to explain what it means to say that humans are relational beings. What is the purpose of Christian morality in light of the relational nature of humans?  </span></em></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB Framework, Option C, I.B.2</span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. The unity of the whole human race (CCC, nos. 842, 1877). </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>a. The social nature of the human person (CCC, nos. 1878-1889, 1929). </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>b. field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">For Grades 10-12 (Recommended)<br /> This lesson presents students with questions regarding the origins of the universe and the act of Creation through God the Father and his Son, Jesus, and it challenges students to consider how science and faith intersect to answer those questions. Students evaluate possible scientific explanations for the circumstances preceding the Big Bang, analyze relevant Scripture, and articulate their thoughts in response to the evidence presented.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong>Prerequisite Knowledge</strong><br /> Students should have prior knowledge of the Big Bang Theory presented in the context of a science course.<br /> Students should have prior knowledge of the Incarnation presented in the context of a theology course.<br /> Students should have prior knowledge of the Trinitarian doctrine of the Church presented in the context of a theology course.<br />  </p> <p><strong>Knowledge</strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Describe possible circumstances that preceded the Big Bang.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Compare and contrast between infinite and finite.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Describe the role of Jesus in Creation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. Articulate that God’s creation was a complete act of love.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>5. Argue that Jesus as the New Adam brings about a New Creation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long theories.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Analysis of Biblical text.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Dialogue with colleagues.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Curiosity and imagination.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Assessing and analysing information.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Effective communication.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 1 (Context of a Science Class) </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span>50 minutes</span></em></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How do scientists explain the origin of the universe?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Use Pre-Quiz to assess student knowledge of Big Bang.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1nwYjxQYEYAD1rsomy-K5T1XRziMsR3wOdByAg0iOVFM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Google Doc - Pre-quiz: Student knowledge of Big Bang</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> What is the Big Bang Theory? </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Review premise of Big Bang theory via brief discussion or using video below.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><a href="https://youtu.be/HdPzOWlLrbE"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Origins of the Universe 101 | National Geographic</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Address student misconceptions from pre-quiz.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What existed before the Big Bang?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pose question for students and explain challenges of answering the question.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discuss possible answers to question.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Optional video: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://youtu.be/dr6nNvw55C4"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What happened before the Big Bang?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students record brief notes: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1wGNw-Z79m8PkOpbKch-_y2HU7C5AuzfyWSqEpvTkqQY/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Google Doc - What happened before the Big Bang</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What do we do with this information?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Think, Pair, Share: Have students record their own reactions to today’s discussion; encourage them to consider the implications of these theories in the greater context of finding meaning in life.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students pair up and discuss their reactions. Select a few students to share with the class. Discuss.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Exit Ticket: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://padlet.com/wlundy1/n91o35tjvzc9j57a"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Padlet - How do you think God fits into this?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teachers - Make a copy (Remake) of this padlet to use as a template for your own work.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Use this question to prepare students for the next lesson.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Select and discuss responses.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 2 (Context of a Theology Class) </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span>50 minutes</span></em></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><em><span>Opening Prayer Isaiah 60:1-3</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><a href="https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1JZvdKXLi7RAvnGRptdOlrwnBGIhzrIz_nswkxQGtl6Q/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Google Slides - Before the Beginning</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> Start with Day 2 of the Google SlideShow.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Present the learning essential question: What is the difference between the act of creating and being creative? (10 Min)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students pair up in pairs or small groups and develop an answer to the above question.  Students record answers/thoughts in a notebook to be shared for later.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Student demonstration to define the word “create.”</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Select two students to come before the class and give each a box.  One box contains modeling clay and the other box will remain empty. Without telling students the contents of the boxes, instruct each student to create a bowl using the contents of their box.  Obviously one student will be able to create a bowl while the other student will not. Use this lighthearted activity to demonstrate the definition of creation and explain that humans cannot create something out of nothing. (5 Min)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What do the Scriptures say about Jesus’ role in Creation? (30 Min)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students explore assigned Scriptures and write 2-3 sentence summaries.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Genesis 1: 26</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Colossians 1:16-17 </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>John 1:1, 3, 14</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Hebrews 7:3</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Move between groups to assist and monitor progress.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Next merge all the groups to discuss findings and how they shape understanding of Jesus before creation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Exit Ticket - </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://padlet.com/wlundy1/o3bjrkky06cd74tj"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Padlet: Jesus as the New Adam, Jesus as the First Atom</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students answer questions on Padlet with thoughts from lesson.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>In the beginning...What was before “The beginning”?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What existed before the big bang?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Select and discuss responses.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teachers - Make a copy (Remake) of this padlet to use as a template for your own work.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 3 (Context of a Theology Class) </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span>50 minutes</span></em></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Begin with Prayer, </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>The Canticle of Creatures</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>. </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="http://www.clintonfranciscans.com/images/7.%20July%20-%20Holland.pdf"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Canticle of the Creatures</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <ul> <li><a href="https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1JZvdKXLi7RAvnGRptdOlrwnBGIhzrIz_nswkxQGtl6Q/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Google Slides - Before the Beginning</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> Start with Day 3 of the Google SlideShow.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Present learning essential questions: Did God need to create? Why did God create?  (Approx 10 Min)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students discuss questions in pairs/small groups.  Students write answers/thoughts in a notebook. Select students to share and discuss with class.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Present Church teachings: “God had no need to create…”(CCC 293).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>So why then did God create?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Give time for students to discuss.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>God is complete without creation; He does not </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>need</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> creation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> “God created all things ‘not to increase His glory [for that is impossible] but to show it forth and communicate it’”135 (CCC 293). </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Creation is an act of love</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why did He do it? The motive for this sharing of His glory is pure unselfish love. “God has no other reason for creating than His love and goodness” (CCC 293).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>So why was Jesus sent by the Father?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students discuss in small groups, then bring ideas to large group discussion. facilitated by the teacher.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Present Church teaching. God’s love culminates in His act of salvation, the redemption of humanity. In this act, Jesus becomes the 2nd Adam.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>This is the beginning of the New Creation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Closing </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://padlet.com/wlundy1/9kkjf580y9q0a93"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Padlet: What does Jesus as the New Adam mean for all of humanity?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teachers - </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Remake - </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Make a copy of this padlet to use as a template for your own work.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Cumulative Assignment:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Assign students to write 1-2 paragraphs in response to the following questions:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is your opinion about creation? Give evidence and reasons to support your opinion from both of the domains of science and theology.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>In answering the question above, which domain (science or theology) do you find more compelling? Give reasons to support your answer.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Ybr4KQ8UlEkb27WrbEayzYuQvcgBRVEiEwdWhJZY-YM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Writing Prompt</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> and </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1OQS_ZjvAF6DvKYkoC65Xh3heBdMSlybP3U8xZ2owPMM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Grading Rubric</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> (Includes scaffolded notes page). </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>This may be used as a cross-curricular summative assessment. Students analyze and evaluate scientific and theological explanations for the beginning of time.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 1</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1nwYjxQYEYAD1rsomy-K5T1XRziMsR3wOdByAg0iOVFM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Google Doc - Pre-quiz: Student knowledge of Big Bang</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> - Assess student knowledge of Big Bang. field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson challenges students to explore how science and religion can be integrated by increasing their understandings of the Earth&#039;s origin and its cultural implications. Activities include researching various origin stories; comparing and contrasting Genesis and the Big Bang Theory; and creating their own origin story through religious and scientific lenses. </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span>Purpose of origin stories</span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>Both science and faith have worked to understand the beginning of life on Earth</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>The Earth’s scientific origin story (the big bang theory) is aligned with Catholic teaching</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>The principles of the Christian origin story</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>Scientific understandings are constantly changing</span></span></span></p> <p>Genesis story</p> <p>Big Bang Theory</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>Make observations</p> <p><span><span><span><span>Reflect on their personal origin stories </span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span>Use written and oral language to communicate these reflections</span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span>Compare and contrast various origin explanations</span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p dir="ltr">Day 1</p> <p dir="ltr">Activator: Students will begin class by responding to the question "How did I come to be here in class today?" in their journal.  Afterward, students will be asked to volunteer their ideas by writing them on the whiteboard. As a class, we will annotate the students' responses - circling the answers based on faith and underlining the responses based on science.  </p> <p>Activity: <strong>Origin Story Graphic Organizer </strong>(bold terms represent resources already created and found in the resource tab).  Students will research various culture’s story regarding the creation of the Earth.</p> <p>Day 2</p> <p dir="ltr">Review: Process Origin Stories from the day before: What do they teach us about human beings and our origins?</p> <p>Activity:<strong> Envelope Activity.  </strong>Students will be placed in groups of 4 and will be given an envelope full of images and terms they can and/or cannot use.  Each envelope represents a different time period in the modern world.  Students will be asked to answer "How do day and night occur" using the guidelines found in each envelope.  They will either share their stories orally or using the whiteboards (based on their time period) in preparation for the class discussion.</p> <p>Class Discussion:  Each group will present their answer to the activator question.  As a group, the class will discuss the differences in each story as it relates to the time period.  The class will hopefully conclude that as our knowledge increases so does our ability to describe the world around us (an evolution of understanding!).</p> <p>Lecture<strong>: Origin Story Lecture. </strong>Please note that some materials for Day 3 and Day 4 can be found in this lecture. </p> <p>Day 3</p> <p>Activator: Snowball Activity.  Ask students the question, “What have you learned these past two days?”  Students will write down their responses, crumble up the paper into a snowball, and throw it across the room.  Each student will then pick up another snowball and read it to the class.</p> <p dir="ltr">Activity: Think Pair Share.  Students will work in pairs to read either Genesis 1 and 2 or a <strong>Big Bang Theory article</strong>.  They will then explain their readings to their partner.</p> <p>Day 4</p> <p>Activator:<strong> Watch Being a Religious Scientist </strong>Video &amp; discuss.</p> <p>Activity: <strong>Origin Story Assignment:</strong> Where did you come from? Students will spend class time creating their own origin story.  This will also be their final assessment for the lesson.</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong>Origin Story Assignment:</strong> Where did you come from? (see resources for assignment outline and rubric). </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><em>NGSS (Science &amp; Engineering Practices)</em></p> <p>Asking Questions and Defining Problems.Constructing Explanations and Designing Solutions.</p> <p><em>ACT College Readiness Standards</em></p> <p>Make a scientific claim &amp; Use evidence to support a claim (EMI 602)</p> <p><em>Archdiocese of Chicago. Religion Curriculum Goals</em></p> <p>Creed: Understand, believe and proclaim the Triune God as revealed in the signs of creation, Sacred Scripture, CatholicTradition and human experience. (NDC pp. 45-46, 75-78, 83-86, 91-93, 97-98)</p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder text-formatted field field--name-comment-body field--type-text-long field--label-hidden field__item"><p>This is an excellent lesson plan that is ready to go. Everything a teacher needs to get started has been provided and then some. The plan creates an equitable and active learning environment, as well as high expectations. The video with Mayim Bialik “Science and Religion” is very helpful. Students familiar with “The Big Bang Theory” TV program will immediately find a relatable personality who professes to being both religious and a scientist. Furthermore, since Mayim is Jewish her comments would have a broader appeal to other than Catholic students. But for the purposes of Catholic students, it is suggested that a video with Bro. Guy Consolmagno (Youtube Part II: A Vatican Scientist) be used as well.</p> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/contrib/bootstrap_barrio/templates/field/field--text-long.html.twig' --> field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">Students will examine creation from multiple perspectives--the Biblical accounts in Genesis 1-2, and the scientific account of the history of the Earth.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>1. Students will learn what a myth is.</li> <li>2. Why is myth a valid form of knowledge?</li> <li>3. What is a scientific fact?</li> <li>4. How is Genesis 1-2 truth told in a mythic mode?</li> <li>5. What does Genesis 1-2 teach about creation?</li> <li>6. What does science teach about creation?</li> <li>7. Is one type of knowledge better than another.</li> <li>8. Biblical interpretation in a contextual approach.</li> <li>9. What is a biblical commentary?</li> <li>10. How to use a biblical commentary.</li> <li>11. Draw the cosmology of the ancient Jewish view of creation.</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>1. Compare creation stories to see any commonalities.</li> <li>2. How is scientific explanation different.</li> <li>3. Is one form of knowledge better than the other. Why?</li> <li>4. Learn the connection of the Enuma Elish and Epic of Gilgamesh to Genesis 1-2.</li> <li>5. What is the biblical author of Genesis 1-2 teaching about creation?</li> <li>6. What is a contextual interpretation of the bible?</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>1. Input on types of knowledge. Explain the importance of symbol, metaphor, and analogy to Science and theology.</li> <li>2. Explain what a myth is (i.e. not a falsehood).</li> <li>3. Compare other Creation myths to Genesis. What might these be saying about the cultures they come from?</li> <li>4. What points is the biblical author making about Genesis in a literal interpretation and a contextual interpretation?</li> <li>5. Ask students if there are things that are not believable in the Genesis account. Why or why not?</li> <li>6. What is the scientific account of creation?</li> <li>7. How do the accounts differ in 5 and 6?</li> <li>8. Make the point of both ways of viewing creation are valid but different. Use the comparison of apples or oranges.</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Formative assessment: <ul> <li>1. Research Creation story of another culture and write out a summary. Write out a comparison to Genesis.</li> <li>2. Write out a reflection on what the non-Genesis creation story is saying about its understanding of creation.</li> <li>3. Quiz on theology of Genesis 1-2.</li> <li>4. Homework questions from textbook on Genesis 1-2.</li> <li>5. Find a piece of artwork that reflects creation and write out why you chose this piece of art.</li> </ul> </li> <li>Summative assessment: <ul> <li>1. Test on all of the points in content section.</li> <li>2. Write their own creation story using the points made by the biblical author.</li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Catholic Diocese of Wilmington, DE standards: <ul> <li>1. Read and Interpret Sacred Scripture within the tradition and teaching of the Church.</li> <li>2. Give attention to what human authors say and what God reveals by their work.</li> <li>3. Take into account the conditions of the time when it was written and culture where it was written.</li> <li>4. Read and interpret each part of Sacred Scripture with an awareness and understanding of the unity of the content and teaching of the entire Bible.</li> <li>5. Be attentive to the analogy of faith, that is, the unity that exists in all Church teaching.</li> <li>6. The Church teaches how to relate truths of faith to Science.</li> <li>7. There can be no conflict between religious truth and scientific and historical truth.</li> <li>8. Other forms of literature in the Bible.</li> <li>9. The difference between the Catholic understanding of Scripture and the fundamentalist view of Scripture.</li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder callback="flag.link_builder:build" arguments="0=node&amp;1=60&amp;2=favorite_lessons" token="jN_NZm9rBnstYP7-ErTPcPYKjRkHTX4fdpWby16z05s"></drupal-render-placeholder> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-resources--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-resources.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-resources.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-resources field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Lesson Resources</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>1. The Bible.</li> <li>2. The internet for creation stories, i.e., Enuma Elish and Gilgamesh</li> <li>3. Biology teacher for the scientific account of creation.</li> <li>4. DVD on cosmic origins from the Magis center.</li> <li>5. TextbookUnderstanding the Old Testament or equivalent</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-questions--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-questions.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-questions.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-questions field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Essential Questions</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li>What are creation stories?</li> <li>Do many cultures have a creation story?</li> <li>What is the literary form called a myth? Why is this literary form valid?</li> <li>Is Genesis factually true? If not, does it contain other types of truths?</li> <li>What is the scientific earth story?</li> <li>How does one interpret the Bible?</li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--comment--comment-body--comment.html.twig * field--comment--comment-body.html.twig * field--comment--comment.html.twig * field--comment-body.html.twig x field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/contrib/bootstrap_barrio/templates/field/field--text-long.html.twig' --> <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-comment-body field--type-text-long field--label-hidden field__item"><p>This is a very good lesson plan written from the perspective of the theology/religion teacher. The lesson plan will provide an equitable learning environment, establish a fairly high expectation, an active learning environment, and answer the essential questions. It would be helpful, however, to adjust or wordsmith the "Essential Question." Rather than "Do many cultures have a creation story?", which is somewhat rhetorical; it is recommended that it be restated as, "Provide examples of creation stories." Second, under the "Skills" and "Lesson Resources" sections, comparisons with the "Enuma Elish" is a good and necessary choice, but it should be noted that the Gilgamesh Epic is a Flood Narrative, not a Creation Report. In lieu of the Gilgamesh Epic, it would be good to compare the biblical account with the Hymn to Ptah and the Hymn of Atum, the Egyptian creation myths.</p> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">Students will outline their basic understanding of evolutionary theory and discuss any conflicts or contradictions they believe exist with Catholic Theology and Sacred Scripture. Then the difference between the Catholic and Fundamentalist approach to Scripture will be outlined and, with the knowledge of how the Catholic Tradition approaches Scripture, they will delve into the primary source of Scripture to see what Genesis actually says.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Students will be able to define the Catholic approach to Scripture.</li> <li>They will beable to outline the more-than-literal truths in Scripture.</li> <li>They will see, when approaching Scripture as Catholics (and many Protestants) do, there is no conflict whatsoever between their faith and the reality of evolution.</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Biblical Exegesis</li> <li>Collaboration</li> <li>Critical Thinking</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li>Have students write out their understanding of evolution.</li> <li>Then, have the students write out any/all conflicts they see with Scripture. They must detail why they see it as a conflict too.</li> <li>Small GroupWork - Have the students gather in small groups and share their thoughts. As they discuss, they are to put together a group consensus on how they believe evolution works. This will be guided/monitored by the instructor.</li> <li>Then have students read the Creation Story accounts in Scripture-Genesis 1:1-3:24. Students will list any/all conflicts they see between Scripture and evolution (citing the chapter and verse of each conflict) as well as explaining why those issues count as conflicts.</li> <li>Have each group share their definitions of evolution as well as the conflicts they found with the class as a whole.</li> <li>Define (or review, depending on the previous experience with exegesis of the students in the class) the Catholic and the Fundamentalist approach to reading Scripture.</li> <li>Large Group Discussion - <ul> <li>What differences may these approaches yield in the life of believers?</li> <li>Which approach they find more appealing?</li> <li>Why do they see it like this?</li> </ul> </li> <li>Ask the students which approach to Scripture the Catholic Church utilizes.</li> <li>Outline the truths we find in Genesis when we look at it through the Catholic lens. Depending on how in-depth you want to go, there are several levels you can explore.</li> </ol> <ul> <li>Key Themes - When we look to Genesis we see <ol> <li>God wanted creation and everything is created by God</li> <li>All God created is good</li> <li>God made creation to be in relationship </li> <li>God made humanity “very good” and literally created us to be stewards</li> <li>Evil comes into the world as a result of our own bad choices and our choosing to disobey God.</li> </ol> </li> <li>A little Higher Level conversation: <ol> <li>Adam and Eve are not proper names in Ancient Hebrew</li> <li>Adam means “humanity” or “humankind,”</li> <li>Eve means “life” or “mother of the living,”</li> <li>So, the story of Genesis is what happens when life comes to/is joined with humanity.</li> </ol> </li> <li>A little Higher Level still... <ol> <li>We further see evidence of this as the serpent and the tree were two of the most popular symbols of the chief Canaanite deities.</li> <li>So, for the Hebrews who were settling in Canaan, this story warns that to depart from their God and side with the serpent and the tree is to lose the paradise you have.</li> </ol> </li> <li>10.  Large Group Discussion - Does this make sense? <ul> <li>Can you see how these truths aren’t contingent on a literal reading? They are more than literal truths. Can you see how there is no conflict with evolution, at all? Any questions?</li> </ul> </li> <li>11. Let the students know we will begin our formal study of evolution next class.</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Pre-assessment via their definition of evolution and the conflict they see with Genesis; <ul> <li>diagnostic tool/formative assessment in how well they use and interpret the primary source of Scripture.</li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Sacred Scriptures 1: Divine Revelation: God Speaks to Us <ul> <li>A. God’s self-revelation in words, deeds, covenants</li> <li>B. Transmission of Divine Revelation</li> <li>C. Sacred Scripture</li> <li>D. Faith is our personal and communal response to Revelation</li> </ul> </li> <li>Biology Standard - 3.1.10.C1: Explain the mechanisms of biological evolution.</li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT <span class="comment__time">Sun, 12/08/2019 - 01:46pm <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'rdf_metadata' --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--comment--comment-body--comment.html.twig * field--comment--comment-body.html.twig * field--comment--comment.html.twig * field--comment-body.html.twig x field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/contrib/bootstrap_barrio/templates/field/field--text-long.html.twig' --> <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-comment-body field--type-text-long field--label-hidden field__item"><p>This is a fine lesson plan that attempts to address the alleged conflict between Scripture and Science. The lesson plan makes for both an equitable and active learning environment. There are several suggestions for improvement, however, that might make for a better plan. Starting with the Methods section with the part entitled "Key Themes" states: “Adam and Eve are not proper names in Ancient Hebrew." This overstatement should be avoided. While it is true that 'Adam can be translated as "humankind," both Adam and Eve do refer to individuals (Gen 4:25; 5:1, 3, 4, 5, 1 Chron. 1:1; Tobit 8:6; Wisd 10:1; Sir. 40:1; 49:16; Hos. 6:7). Second, "exegesis" is the critical explanation or interpretation of a text. Under the Skills section, to what degree will students be taught to do biblical exegesis? Third, the lesson plan states that there will be a comparison made between Catholic and Fundamentalist approaches to Genesis. This is a good strategy, since much of the alleged conflict between faith and reason grows out of a misinterpretation of Scripture. It is suggested that the Institute for Creation Research (www.icr.org), which represents the fundamentalist's position, be added to the Resource section. Finally, under the Standards section, there is a discussion dedicated to biological evolution. This is certainly appropriate, but since the Biblical account describes the creation of the cosmos, it would just as important to discuss the evolution of the universe.</p> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/contrib/bootstrap_barrio/templates/field/field--text-long.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder callback="\Drupal\history\HistoryRenderCallback::lazyBuilder" arguments="0=56"
